intermediate
7 min
Confession vs. Testimony: When Two Claim Sole Killing
Comprehensive rulings on testimony in murder cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal effects of confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahadah) when two individuals each claim to have killed the same victim alone, and the wali claims they both did it together.

Core Idea
A confession is binding even if contradicted, but testimony is invalid if the beneficiary denies part of it.

When two men each confess to killing someone alone, and the victim's heir says they both killed him together, the wali may execute both confessors. However, if the same scenario arises through testimony (witnesses), the testimony becomes invalid. This lesson explores the critical distinction between confession and testimony in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the confession scenario
Two men each independently confess that they alone killed the victim. The wali says: 'You both killed him.' The wali may kill both confessors because each confession establishes qisas against the confessor, and the wali's denial of their sole killing does not negate their confession.
The wali is not required to accept the confession as true; he is simply claiming something different.
2
Apply the rule of iqrar
A confession is binding on the confessor even if the person in whose favor the confession is made denies part of it. The confessor's own admission establishes his liability.
The wali's denial of sole killing (i.e., claiming both) does not invalidate the confession because the confessor is not relying on the wali's acceptance.
3
Contrast with testimony
If the same fact is established by testimony (e.g., two sets of witnesses each testify that one man alone killed the victim), and the wali says they both killed him, then the testimony of both sets becomes invalid. This is because the wali's denial of the solitary nature of the killing is a rejection of part of the witnesses' testimony, which invalidates the whole.
Testimony requires the beneficiary to accept it fully; partial denial makes the witness lose credibility.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in confession, the wali can execute both; in testimony, no one can be executed because the evidence collapses.
This highlights the superior weight of iqrar over shahadah in Hanafi law.

الشهادة في القتل
هو الولي المشهود عليه
فإن صدقهما القاتل فالدية لهم أثلاثا وإن كذبهما، فلا شيء لهما، وللآخر ثلث القاتل والمشهود عليه الدية
= لأنهما يجران لأنفسهما نفعا، وهو انقلاب القود ،مالا، وهو عفو منهما ؛ لأنهما زعما أن القصاص قد سقط، وزعمهما معتبر في حق أنفسهما تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٤/٩]
فإن صدقهما إلخ أي إن صدق الشاهدين الوليين القاتل دون الولي المشهود عليه، فالدية لهم أثلاثا، فيكون لكل واحد من الثلاثة ثلث الدية؛ لأن تصديقه لهما إقرار لهما بثلثي الدية فيلزمه لكن يزعمون كلهم أن نصيب الولي المشهود عليه قد سقط بعفوه ، وهو ينكر ، فلا يقبل قولهم عليه وتحول نصيبه أيضا مالا، فوجب عليه كل الدية، وللمنكر ثلثها. (تكملة، عيني)
عن
يصرف
وإن كذبهما إلخ : يعني إن كذب القاتل الشاهدين فلا شيء لهما؛ لأنهما بشهادتهما عليه بالعفو أقرا ببطلان حقهما في القصاص، فصح إقرارهما في حق أنفسهما، وادعيا انقلاب نصيبهما ،مالا فلا تصدق دعواهما إلا ببينة، وللآخر، وهو الولي، ثلث الدية؛ لأن دعواهما العفو عليه وهو ينكر بمنزلة ابتداء العفو عنهما في حقه، فينقلب نصيبه مالا؛ لأن سقوط القصاص مضاف إليهما، وإن صدقهما المشهود عليه ،والقاتل فلا شيء للمشهود عليه، ولهما ثلثا الدية، وإن صدقهما المشهود عليه وحده غرم القاتل ثلث الدية وهو نصيب المشهود عليه لكنه إلى الشاهدين، والقياس أن لا يلزم القاتل شيء. (عيني، فتح، ملا مسكين) يقتص: أي يقتص من الضارب بهذه الشهادة؛ لأن الثابت بالبينة كالثابت ،معاينة قال صاحب "الهداية": وتأويله إذا شهدوا أنه ضربه بشيء جارح رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٦/٢] قال في "الفتح" "الدر": ولا يحتاج الشاهد أن يقول: إنه مات من جراحته ووجهه أن الموت متى وجد عقيب سبب صالح يضاف إليه لا إلى شيء آخر إذا لم يكن في الظاهر سبب آخر، وإن احتمل؛ لأن احتمال خلاف الظاهر لا في الأحكام، كذا في "رد المحتار". في الزمان: بأن شهد أحدهما قتله الخميس، وشهد الآخر: الجمعة رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٦/٢] أو المكان إلخ: أي أو اختلف الشاهدان في مكان القتل بأن شهد أحدهما أن القتل كان في بلد كذا، وشهد الآخر أنه كان في بلد آخر، أو اختلفا في ما وقع به القتل بأن قال أحدهما قتله بالسلاح والآخر: أنه قتله بالعصا، أو قال أحدهما: إنه قتله بالعصا، وقال الآخر: قتله ولكن لم أدر بما ذا قتله. (ملا مسكين بتصرف) بطلت أي بطلت الشهادة في المسائل كلها؛ لأن القتل لا يتكرر ، فالقتل في زمان أو مكان غير القتل في مكان آخر، أو زمان آخر وكذا القتل بآلة غير القتل بآلة أخرى، ويختلف الأحكام باختلاف الآلة، فكان على كل -،

الشهادة في القتل

وقال الولي: قتلتماه جميعا، فله قتلهما، ولو كان مكان الإقرار شهادة لغت.
للمولى قتل المقرين
الشهادة
= قتل شهادة ،فرد، فلم تقبل وكذا لو كمل النصاب على كل قتل منهما لتيقن القاضي بكذب أحد الفريقين وعدم الأولوية بالقبول، بخلاف ما إذا كمل أحد الفريقين دون الآخر حيث يقبل الكامل، ولو شهد أحدهما بالقتل معاينة، والآخر على إقرار القاتل بذلك كان باطلا لاختلاف المشهود به كذا في "الفتح"، قال في "التكملة": ولو قال المؤلف: ولو شهد أربعة بقتل واختلفوا في الزمان والمكان، أو فيما وقع به القتل، أو قالا: قتله بعصا، وقال الآخر: لم ندر بما ذا قتله بطلت لكان أولى؛ لأنه إذا علم بطلان شهادة المثنى عند الاختلاف علم بطلان شهادة الفرد بالطريق الأولى. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۱۸/۹] تجب الدية: أي تجب الدية في ماله استحسانا والقياس أن لا تقبل هذه الشهادة أصلا؛ لأنهما شهدا بقتل مجهول؛ لأن الآلة إذا جهلت فقد جهل القتل وجه الاستحسان أنهما شهدا بقتل مطلق والمطلق ليس بمجمل لإمكان العمل به، فيجب أقل ،موجبه وهو الدية ولا يحمل قولهما: "لم "ندر" على الغفلة بل على أنهما سعيا للدرء المندوب إليه في العقوبات إحسانا للظن بهما، ثم الدية إنما تجب في ماله دون العاقلة؛ لأن الأصل في القتل العمد، فلا تلزم العاقلة لما مرارا، ولأن المطلق يحمل على الكامل، ولا يثبت الخطأ بالشك [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٦/٢] مر (درر) قتله أي زيدا مثلا منفردا عن صاحبه. قتلهما: يعني إذا أقر رجلان أن كل واحد منهما قتل فلانا منفردا، وقال ولي المقتول بل قتلتماه جميعا، فللولي قتلهما؛ لأن كلا منهما أقر بانفراده بكل القتل وبالقصاص عليه، والمقر له صدقه في وجوب القتل عليه أيضا لكن كذبه في انفراده بالقتل، وتكذيب المقر له المقر في بعض ما أقر به لا يبطل إقراره في الباقي؛ لأن ذلك تفسيقه، وفسق المقر لا يمنع صحة إقراره، ولو أقر رجل أنه قتله، وقامت بينته على آخر أنه قتله، وقال الولي: قتله كلاهما، كان له قتل المقر دون المشهود عليه، وإنما قيد بقوله: "قتلتماه"؛ لأنه لو صدقهما لم يكن له قتل واحد منهما؛ لأن تصديقه كل واحد تكذيب للآخر؛ لأن كل واحد منهما يدعي الانفراد بالقتل، فتصديقه يوجب ذلك، فصار كأنه قال لكل واحد منهما قتلته وحدك ولم يشاركك فيه أحد، ولو قال لأحد المقرين: صدقت أنت قتلته وحدك، كان له قتله. (فتح)
يوجب
مكان الإقرار إلخ أي لو كان في هذه المسألة مكان الإقرار الشهادة بأن شهد اثنان على رجل أنه قتل فلانا، وشهد آخران على آخر أنه قتله وقال الولي: قتلتماه جميعا، لغت الشهادة؛ لأن تكذيب المشهود له الشاهد في بعض ما شهد به تبطل شهادته، وبهذا يظهر الفرق بين الإقرار والشهادة، والمراد بتكذيبه نفي استقلال كل واحد من المشهود عليهما بالقتل؛ لأنه لما قال: قتلاه لم يثبت القتل لكل منفرد ، فصار مكذبا لكل من البينتين. (عيني، فتح)
Book of Crimes. Testimony in murder. He is the wali (heir) against whom testimony is given. If the killer confirms them, then the blood-money is for them in thirds. And if he denies them, then nothing is for them, and for the other (heir) is one third of the blood-money from the killer and the one against whom testimony is given. (= Because they bring benefit to themselves, which is the conversion of qisas to property, and it is their forgiveness because they claim that qisas has been waived, and their claim is valid regarding themselves. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:114] 'If he confirms them' etc. means if the killer confirms the two witnesses (the two heirs) but not the wali against whom the testimony is given, then the blood-money is for them in thirds: each of the three gets one third of the blood-money because his confirmation of them is an admission of two thirds of the blood-money against him, but they all claim that the share of the wali against whom testimony is given has been waived by his forgiveness, and he denies it. So their statement is not accepted against him, and his share also becomes property, so the entire blood-money is due against him, and the denier gets one third of it. (Takmila, 'Ayni) 'And if he denies them' etc.: If the killer denies the two witnesses, then nothing is for them because by testifying against him regarding forgiveness, they admit the invalidity of their right to qisas; their admission is valid regarding themselves. They claim conversion of their share to property, but their claim is not accepted without evidence. And for the other (the heir) is one third of the blood-money because their claim of forgiveness against him while he denies is like initiating forgiveness from them in his right, so his share becomes property because the dropping of qisas is attributed to them. If the one against whom testimony is given and the killer both confirm them, then nothing for the one against whom testimony is given, and they get two thirds of the blood-money. If only the one against whom testimony is given confirms them, then the killer pays one third of the blood-money, which is the share of the one against whom testimony is given, but it goes to the two witnesses; the analogy is that nothing should be required of the killer. ('Ayni, Fath, Miskin) 'He is subject to retaliation': i.e., the striker is subject to retaliation by this testimony because what is established by evidence is like what is witnessed directly. The author of al-Hidayah said: Its interpretation is when they testify that he struck him with a cutting thing. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:436] In al-Fath and al-Durr it is said: The witness does not need to say that he died from his wound; the reason is that when death occurs immediately after a valid cause, it is attributed to it and not to something else if no other cause is apparent, even if possible, because possibility contrary to appearance is not considered in legal rulings. (Radd al-Muhtar) 'In time': i.e., one witness testifies he killed him on Thursday, and another on Friday. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:436] 'Or place' etc.: i.e., the two witnesses disagree on the place of killing, one says in one city, the other in another; or they disagree on the instrument, one says with a weapon, the other with a stick; or one says with a stick and the other says he killed him but I do not know with what. (Miskin, adapted) 'It becomes invalid': i.e., the testimony becomes invalid in all these cases because killing does not recur; killing at one time or place is different from killing at another time or place, and killing with one instrument is different from killing with another, and rulings differ with different instruments. So each... (Text repeats 'day') Book of Crimes. Testimony in murder. And if they testify that he killed him but say 'we do not know with what he killed him', then the blood-money is obligatory. And if two men each confess that he killed him, and the wali says 'you both killed him', then he may kill them both. And if instead of confession there were testimony, it would be invalid. (For the master to kill the confessors, testimony is a single testimony, so it is not accepted. Similarly, if the full number completes for each killing, because the judge is certain that one of the two groups is lying and there is no priority for acceptance, unlike when one group completes and the other does not, where the complete group is accepted. If one testifies to killing by direct observation and another testifies to the killer's confession, it is invalid due to difference in the subject of testimony. (al-Fath) The completers said: If the author had said: If four testify to a killing and they differ in time, place, or instrument, or two say 'he killed him with a stick' and the other says 'I don't know with what he killed him', it would be invalid; it would be more appropriate because if disagreement invalidates the testimony of two, it invalidates that of one a fortiori. [Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:118] 'The blood-money is obligatory': i.e., it is obligatory from his property by istihsan; the analogy is that this testimony should not be accepted at all because they testify to an unknown killing (since if the instrument is unknown, the killing is unknown). The reason for istihsan is that they testify to an absolute killing, and the absolute is not vague because it can be acted upon, so the least of its requirements is due, which is blood-money. And their statement 'we do not know' is not taken as negligence but as their effort for the recommended avoidance in punishments, thinking well of them. Then the blood-money is due from his property, not from the 'aqila, because the basis in intentional killing is not binding on the 'aqila as repeated previously, and because the absolute is interpreted as complete, and error is not established by doubt. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:436] It has passed. (Durar) 'He killed him': i.e., Zayd alone. 'Kill them both': If two men each confess that he killed so-and-so alone, and the wali says 'you both killed him', then the wali may kill them both because each confesses to the entire killing alone, and the confessee confirms him regarding the obligation of killing, but he denies his being alone in the killing. The confessee's denial of part of what the confessor admits does not invalidate the rest of his admission because that is his transgression, and the transgression of the confessor does not prevent the validity of his admission. If a man confesses that he killed him, and evidence is established against another that he killed him, and the wali says 'both killed him', then he may kill the confessor but not the one against whom evidence is given. He specifically said 'you both killed him' because if he confirmed them, he could not kill either because his confirmation of each is a denial of the other, since each claims sole killing; so his confirmation would require that, and it becomes as if he said to each 'you alone killed him' and no one else. If he says to one of the confessors 'you are truthful, you killed him alone', then he may kill him. (Fath) 'Instead of confession, testimony' etc.: If in this case, instead of confession there is testimony — that two testify against one man that he killed so-and-so, and two others testify against another that he killed him, and the wali says 'you both killed him' — the testimony is invalid because the denial of the witness by the one in whose favor testimony is given regarding part of his testimony invalidates his testimony. Thus the difference between confession and testimony is clear. The meaning of his denial is the negation of each one's independence in the killing because when he says 'both killed him', the killing is not established for each individually, so he becomes a denier of each of the two pieces of evidence. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a series of rulings on testimony (shahadah) in murder cases. It begins by defining the scenario where two witnesses testify against the wali (heir of the victim), claiming that he forgave the killer, thereby converting the right of qisas (retaliation) into blood-money (diyah). The ruling has three sub-scenarios depending on the killer's response: if he confirms the testimony, the blood-money is divided into thirds among the testifying witnesses (who are also heirs) and the denying heir; if he denies, the witnesses get nothing and the other heir gets one third; if the wali himself confirms, his share becomes property for the witnesses. The commentary explains the legal reasoning: the witnesses' testimony is an admission against themselves that their right to qisas is invalid, so they cannot then claim diyah unless the killer confirms. Next, the passage covers testimony that the defendant struck the victim and he died from it, ruling that retaliation (qisas) is established. The commentary clarifies that the death is attributed to the strike if it occurs immediately after a valid cause, even if the witness does not explicitly state that death resulted from the injury. Then, it addresses disagreement between witnesses regarding the time, place, or instrument of killing: if they differ on any of these, the testimony is invalid because each killing is unique and cannot be the same event. Similarly, if one witness says he was killed with a stick and the other says 'I don't know', the testimony is invalid. However, if both witnesses say 'we don't know with what he killed him', the blood-money is obligatory by istihsan (juristic preference), contrary to strict analogy (qiyas) which would reject the testimony as vague. The reason is that their testimony establishes an absolute killing, and the least obligation (blood-money) is imposed. Finally, the passage discusses the case of two men each confessing to killing the same person alone, and the wali claims both killed him together. In this case, the wali may kill both confessors because each confession is valid for qisas against the confessor, and the wali's denial of their solitary killing does not negate their confession. But if the same scenario arises through testimony (not confession), the testimony is invalid because the witnesses contradict each other when the wali says both killed him. The commentary distinguishes between confession and testimony: in confession, the confessor's admission is effective even if the wali denies part, while in testimony, the wali's denial of part invalidates the whole testimony.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Confession by a party, which is binding on the confessor even if contradicted by others.
الشهادة (al-shahādah): Testimony given by witnesses in a murder case, which may establish qisas or diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between confession and testimony in the scenario where two individuals claim sole killing and the wali says both killed him?
A) Both lead to the same outcome: execution of both.
B) Confession leads to execution of both, testimony leads to invalidity.
C) Confession is only valid if the wali confirms it.
D) Testimony is stronger than confession in this case.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a confession is binding on the confessor even when the beneficiary denies its exclusivity, but testimony is invalidated by such denial.

Hunting Rulings: The Decisive Moment of Shooting
Explains rulings on hunting when shooter's status changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the state at the time of shooting determines the ruling for hunted game, and explain the intra-Hanafi exception for apostasy.

Core Idea
The moment of shooting, not the strike, decides permissibility and penalty for hunting.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi hunting law: the decisive moment is when the arrow is released, not when it hits. This affects cases where the hunter's status changes between release and impact. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi difference regarding apostasy after shooting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states that the ruling on game depends on the shooter's state at the time of shooting (ramy), not when the arrow strikes. Understand that shooting is considered the effective slaughter (dhabh).
This is the agreed-upon principle in the Hanafi school.
2
Apply to conversion scenarios
A Muslim who apostatizes after shooting still yields lawful game; a non-Muslim who converts after shooting does not. Verify that in both cases the state at shooting is decisive.
3
Apply to ihram scenarios
A muhrim who shoots and then becomes halal before the arrow hits owes the penalty. A halal person who shoots and then enters ihram before the arrow hits owes no penalty. Again, the state at shooting determines the penalty.
The penalty (jazaa) is for the transgression of hunting while in ihram.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi exception
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani deviate from the strict time-of-shooting rule in one case: if a Muslim shoots and then apostatizes, they still consider the game permissible based on the initial valid act 'making it permissible'. Understand their reasoning.
This is a recognized exception; the ruling outcome is the same as under the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحل الصيد بردة الرامي لا بإسلامه، ووجب الجزاء بحله لا بإحرامه بعد الرمي لا يحل اعتبار حالة القتل محرم بعد الرمي بعد الرمي وحل الصيد إلخ : معناه: إذا رمى مسلم صيدا، فارتد قبل وقوع السهم الصيد، حل أكله، ولو رماه وهو مجوسي، فأسلم قبل وقوع السهم لا يحل؛ لأن المعتبر حالة الرمي في حق الحل والحرمة؛ إذ الرمي هو الذكاة؛ لأنه فعله، ويدخل وقت قدرته لا الإصابة فتعتبر الأهلية، وعدمها عند الرمي تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/٩] ووجب الجزاء إلخ أي لو رمى المحرم صيدا، فحل قبل الإصابة ثم أصاب، وجب عليه الجزاء، وإن رماه وهو حلال، فأحرم قبل الإصابة، فوقع الصيد، وهو محرم، لا يجب عليه الجزاء؛ لأن الجزاء يجب بالتعدي، وهو الرمي في حالة الإحرام، ووجد ذلك في الأول دون الثاني، والأصل في مسائل هذا الكتاب: أن يعتبر وقت الرمي بالاتفاق، وإنما عدل أبو يوسف ومحمد عن ذلك فيما إذا رمى إلى مسلم فارتد - والعياذ بالله - قبل الإصابة باعتبار أنه صار مبرئا له على ما بينا في أول هذا الفصل، والله تعالى أعلم. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/٩]
And the game becomes permissible by the apostasy of the shooter, not by his Islam; and the penalty becomes obligatory by his becoming free of ihram (halal), not by his ihram. After shooting, it does not become permissible. Consideration is of the state at the time of killing. Muhrim after shooting, after shooting. 'And the game becomes permissible, etc.' means: If a Muslim shoots at game and then apostatizes before the arrow strikes the game, it is permissible to eat it. If a Zoroastrian shoots at it and then becomes Muslim before the arrow strikes, it is not permissible. Because what is considered in terms of permissibility and prohibition is the state at the time of shooting, since the shooting is the effective slaughter (dhakat); because it is his action, and the time of his ability and not the time of hitting enters, so capacity and its absence are considered at the time of shooting. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/125). 'And the penalty becomes obligatory, etc.' means: If a muhrim shoots at game and then becomes free of ihram (halal) before the arrow hits, then the game is hit, the penalty is obligatory upon him. If he shoots while halal and then enters ihram before the arrow hits, then the game falls while he is muhrim, the penalty is not obligatory upon him because the penalty becomes obligatory by transgression, which is shooting while in the state of ihram, and that is found in the first case but not the second. The principle in the issues of this book is that the time of shooting is considered by agreement. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad only deviated from that in the case of a Muslim who shoots and then apostatizes - God forbid - before the arrow strikes, because it is considered that he has made it permissible as we explained at the beginning of this chapter. And God Almighty knows best. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 9/125)
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) explains two rulings related to hunting. First, the permissibility of consuming hunted game depends on the shooter's state at the moment of shooting, not when the arrow strikes. If a Muslim shoots and then apostatizes, the game is lawful because the effective act (the shooting) was done by a Muslim. Conversely, if a Zoroastrian shoots and then converts to Islam before the arrow hits, the game is not lawful because at the time of shooting he was not a Muslim. Second, the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) who hunts is obligatory if he was in ihram at the time of shooting, even if he becomes halal by the time the arrow hits. But if he shoots while halal and then enters ihram before the arrow strikes, no penalty is due. The general rule is that the time of shooting is the decisive moment. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani made an exception: if a Muslim shoots and then apostatizes before the arrow strikes, they consider the game permissible because the initial state of the shooter made it licit. This exception is based on the idea that the shooter has 'made it permissible' by his initial valid state.

Key Terms
رمى (ramā): The act of shooting an arrow or projectile at game.
صيد (ṣayd): Game animal that is hunted.
محرم (muḥrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, during which hunting is prohibited.
جزاء (jazā'): The penalty (usually sacrifice or compensation) for a muhrim who hunts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a hunter shoots an arrow while in ihram and then becomes halal before the arrow hits the game, what is the ruling regarding the penalty?
A) No penalty is due because the game was struck while he was halal.
B) The penalty is due because the shooting occurred while he was in ihram.
C) The penalty is due only if he intended to hunt.
D) The penalty is waived because he became halal.

Key Takeaway
The state of the shooter at the moment of release determines both the permissibility of the game and the liability for penalty.

Diyah for Shibh al-Amd: The Sahibayn vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyat composition for shibh al-amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the composition of diyat for shibh al-amd and explain the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
The diyat of shibh al-amd is 100 camels, but its division into age groups is disputed within the Hanafi school.

The diyat (blood money) for quasi-intentional killing (shibh al-amd) is fixed at 100 camels. However, the Hanafi school has an internal dispute on how those 100 camels should be categorized by age. The relied-upon view (sahibayn) divides them into four equal groups of 25, while Imam Muhammad in one narration requires a different distribution including pregnant camels. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its amount
Note that diyat for shibh al-amd is 100 camels, same as for intentional killing, but the distribution differs.
Diyah for khata' (accidental) is 100 camels in fifths (20 each).
2
State the sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the sahibayn), the 100 camels are divided into four equal categories: 25 bint makhad, 25 bint labun, 25 hiqqa, 25 jadha'a.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
State the opposing view of Muhammad (in one riwaya)
Imam Muhammad also has a transmission where he holds: 30 hiqqa, 30 jadha'a, and 40 thaniyya (camels in their sixth year) that are all pregnant (khalifa).
Shafi‘i and Ahmad agree with this view.
4
Examine the hadith evidence for each
The sahibayn rely on a hadith: the Prophet judged diyat as 100 camels 'in quarters' (أرباعا), which cannot be for accidental killing (which is in fifths). Muhammad's view relies on a hadith: '40 from thaniyya to bazil, all pregnant.'
Both hadith are considered authentic; the dispute is over which one to apply.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the sahibayn's view (25 each). This is the ruling presented first in the matn and is considered the stronger riwaya.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is the actual animals required for payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دية شبه العمد مائة من الإبل أرباعا من بنت مخاض إلى جذعة، ولا تغليظ إلا في الإبل، والخطأ مائة من الإبل أخماسا : ابن مخاض وبنت مخاض وبنت لبون وحقة وجذعة، دية الخطأ عشرون عشرون عشرون عشرون عشرون كتاب الديات: الديات جمع دية، وهي في اللغة مصدر، ودى القاتل المقتول أعطى ديته وأعطى لوليه المال الذي هو بدل النفس، ثم قيل لذلك المال : الدية تسمية بالمصدر كذا في "المغرب"، وفي الشرع: عبارة عما يؤدي، وقد صار هذا الاسم علما على بدل النفوس دون غيرها، وهو الأرش، وإنما سمي بدل النفس دية؛ لأنه يؤدي عادة؛ لأنه قلما يجري فيه العفو؛ لعظم حرمة الآدمي، ثم ذكر الديات بعد الجنايات ظاهر المناسبة لما أن الدية أحد موجي الجناية في الآدمي صيانة له عن القصاص، لكن لما كان معنى الإحياء في القصاص أكثر، قدم بيان القود على الدية. تكملة، فتح، ملا مسكين) مائة من الإبل، الإبل إلخ: أي دية شبه العمد مائة من الإبل أرباعا من بنت مخاض، وهي التي طعنت في السنة الثانية إلى جذعة، وهي التي طعنت في الخامسة، وتكون خمس وعشرون بنت مخاض، وخمس وعشرون بنت لبون، وخمس وعشرون حقة، وخمس وعشرون جذعة، وهذا عندهما وعند محمد ثلاثون حقة، وثلاثون جذعة، وأربعون ثنية في بطونها أولادها؛ لقوله عليه: "ألا إن قتيل خطأ العمد بالسوط والعصا ،والحجر، وفيه دية مغلظة مائة ، من أربعون منها من ثنية إلى بازل عامها كلهن خلفة، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية، ولهما: أن النبي عليه قضى في الدية بمائة من الإبل ،أرباعا، ومعلوم أنه لم يرد به الخطأ؛ لأنها تجب فيه أحماسا، فعلم أن المراد به شبه العمد والثني من الإبل ما استكمل السنة الخامسة ودخل في السادسة، والبازل ما دخل في السنة التاسعة، والذكر والأنثى فيه سواء، والخلفة الحامل من النوق. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٨/٢]
The diyat of quasi-intentional killing is one hundred camels in quarters (four categories) from bint makhad to jadha'a, and no increase except in camels. And the accidental killing is one hundred camels in fifths: ibn makhad, bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, and jadha'a. Diyat of accidental killing: twenty, twenty, twenty, twenty, twenty. The Book of Diyat: diyat is plural of diya... (definition repeated). One hundred camels, etc.: i.e., the diyat of quasi-intentional killing is one hundred camels in quarters from bint makhad (which has entered its second year) to jadha'a (which has entered its fifth year). So there are twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqa, and twenty-five jadha'a. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). But according to Muhammad: thirty hiqqa, thirty jadha'a, and forty thaniyya with their young in their wombs—due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Indeed, the killed by quasi-intentional (line of accident) with whip, stick, and stone—its diyat is heavy: one hundred, of which forty are from thaniyya to bazil, all of them khalifa (pregnant).' And al-Shafi‘i and Ahmad in one narration said similarly. And for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged diyat as one hundred camels in quarters, and it is known that he did not intend accidental killing because that is obligated in fifths, so it is understood that the intended is quasi-intentional. And thaniyya of camels is that which has completed its fifth year and entered the sixth; bazil is that which entered the ninth year; the male and female are equal therein; and khalifa is the pregnant she-camel.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that diyat for shibh al-amd is 100 camels divided into four equal quarters of 25 each: bint makhad (2-year-old), bint labun (3-year-old), hiqqa (4-year-old), and jadha'a (5-year-old). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the sahibayn). The commentary then presents Imam Muhammad's own differing view in a riwaya: 30 hiqqa, 30 jadha'a, and 40 thaniyya (camels in their sixth year) that are all pregnant. He supports this with a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) prescribed for shibh al-amd a diyat of 100 camels, 40 of which should be thaniyya to bazil (9-year-old) and all pregnant. The commentary notes that Shafi‘i and Ahmad agree with Muhammad. For the sahibayn, they rely on another hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) judged diyat as 100 camels in quarters, which cannot refer to accidental killing (khata’) because that is in fifths, so it must be shibh al-amd. The passage also defines the ages of camels and mentions that the male and female are equal in value for diyat.

Key Terms
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Killing that resembles intentional but without intent to kill, e.g., striking with a stick or whip.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A she-camel that has entered its second year.
جذعة (jadh‘a): A she-camel that has entered its fifth year.
ثنية (thaniyya): A camel that has completed its fifth year and entered the sixth.
خلفة (khalifa): A pregnant she-camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) composition of diyat for shibh al-amd in the Hanafi school?
A) 30 hiqqa, 30 jadha'a, 40 thaniyya (all pregnant).
B) 20 each of five types.
C) 25 each of bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, and jadha'a.
D) 100 gold dinars.

Key Takeaway
The diyat for shibh al-amd is 100 camels; the Hanafi school relies on the division into four equal quarters (25 each) as per the sahibayn, though a minority view within the school requires a different distribution with pregnant camels.

No Increase (Tashdeed) Except in Camels
States the rule that the heavy diyat is only in camels, not other forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the heavy diyat (taghliz) applies only when the payment is in camels, and explain why other forms of payment do not attract the increase.

Core Idea
Heavy diyat is exclusive to camels — fixed measures come only from revelation, not reason.

In this lesson, we examine a concise but significant rule from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the heavy diyat (taghliz) is only applicable when the blood money is paid in camels. The commentator provides the rationale: the sacred law and consensus have specified camels, and such fixed measures are solely derived from textual sources, not independent reasoning. This lesson will clarify why this restriction matters and how it affects judicial rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the rule explicitly: 'No increase (taghliz) except in camels.' This means the heavy diyat (100 camels in fifths) is only triggered when the payment is made in camels.
The matn phrase 'ولاتغليظ إلخ' is abbreviated; the commentary expands it.
2
Understand the basis in revelation and consensus
The commentator gives two proofs: the sacred law came with it (camels) and there is consensus (ijma) on this. The heavy diyat is a fixed measure that cannot be analogized.
Fixed measures (muqaddarat) are known only by hearing (sam‘), not by reason (ra'y).
3
Examine the epistemological principle
Recognize that such fixed amounts are tawqifiyyah — determined by divine text. Human reasoning has no role in modifying or extending them.
This principle prevents qiyas on texts that set specific numeric values or types.
4
Consider the consequence of a contrary ruling
If a judge were to rule that the heavy diyat applies to gold or silver, his judgement would be void (la yanfudh) because it lacks authoritative textual specification (tawqif).
The nullity shows the binding nature of the revealed measure.
5
Apply the rule to practice
Today, diyat is often paid in cash. The heavy diyat is not applied to cash payments because the text specifies camels. Only the standard amount (value of 100 camels) is due.
This highlights the continued relevance of classical rulings even when the medium changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تغليظ إلخ لأن الشرع ورد به وعليه الإجماع والمقدرات لا تعرف إلا سماعا؛ إذ لا مدخل للرأي فيها، فلم تتغلظ بغيره حتى لو قضى به القاضي لا ينفذ قضاؤه؛ لعدم التوقيف بالتقدير بغير الإبل تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٧/٩]
And no increase etc., because the sacred law has come with it (camels) and there is consensus upon it. And fixed measures are only known by hearing (sam‘); there is no room for reason in them. So it (the diyat) does not become heavy with other (forms of property), such that even if the judge were to judge (increase on gold/silver), his judgement would not be executed due to lack of authoritative specification of the fixed measure by other than camels. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/127.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an expansion_probe on the matn's phrase 'ولا تغليظ إلا في الإبل' (and no increase except in camels). The commentary justifies why the heavy diyat of 100 camels applies only when the payment is in camels, not when it is in gold or silver. The reason is that the sacred law (shar‘) has specifically prescribed camels for the heavy diyat, and there is consensus on this. The amounts of diyat are determined by divine revelation (sam‘), not by human reasoning. Therefore, if a judge were to rule that the heavy diyat applies to gold or silver, his ruling would be invalid because the law has not set a fixed measure for that. The reference to al-Bahr al-Raiq provides the source.

Key Terms
تغليظ (tashdeed / taghliz): Making the diyat heavy or increased in amount or quality (e.g., 100 camels in fifths versus quarters).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the heavy diyat (taghliz) only apply to camels?
A) Because camels are the only valuable property.
B) Because the sacred law specifically prescribed it and there is consensus.
C) Because jurists chose camels by analogy.
D) Because it is easier for the payer.

Key Takeaway
The heavy diyat (taghliz) is exclusively tied to camels as payment, because fixed measures are derived from revelation, not reason.

Diyah for Accidental Killing (Khata') and Its Five Categories
Specifies the composition of diyat for khata' and a dispute with Shafi'i on ibn makhad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi composition of diyat khata' and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that rejects the Shafi'i substitution of ibn labun for ibn makhad.

Core Idea
The diyat of accidental killing is 100 camels in five categories; the Hanafi school insists on ibn makhad based on explicit hadith.

This passage clarifies the exact types of camels required in the diyat for accidental killing (khata') according to the Hanafi school. It cites a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that specifies five categories, including a male camel called ibn makhad. The text then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i agreed with most categories but replaced ibn makhad with ibn labun. The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith is the decisive proof against his view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and composition
Read the statement that diyat khata' is one hundred camels 'in fifths' (ahmas). List the five categories: 20 ibn makhad, 20 bint makhad, 20 bint labun, 20 hiqqa, 20 jadha'a.
Note that 'ahmas' means five equal groups of 20 each.
2
Locate the textual proof
Find the hadith cited from Ibn Mas'ud. It explicitly includes 'twenty ibn makhad' (ذكر). Confirm the narration is from Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi.
The hadith is the primary dalil naqli for the Hanafi position.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i accepts the same categories but replaces ibn makhad with ibn labun. Determine the practical difference: twenty ibn labun instead of twenty ibn makhad.
The objection is based on other possible narrations or qiyas.
4
Apply the Hanafi response and practical consequence
Understand the Hanafi argument that the explicit hadith (hujja) is proof against the Shafi'i view. Relate this to the thamarah al-khilaf: the actual camel type required in diyat payment differs between the schools.
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit text, giving it priority over analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخطأ إلخ: أي دية الخطأ مائة من الإبل أحماسا أي عشرون ابن مخاض وعشرون بنت مخاض وعشرون بنت لبون وعشرون حقة، وعشرون جذعة تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۲۸/۹] لما روى ابن مسعود هم أن النبي [؟] قال: "في دية الخطأ عشرون حقة وعشرون جذعة وعشرون بنت مخاض وعشرون بنت لبون وعشرون ابن مخاض ذكر"، رواه أبو داود والترمذي ،وآخرون والشافعي أخذ بمذهبنا غير أنه قال: يجب عشرون ابن لبون مكان ابن مخاض والحديث حجة عليه رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٨/٢]
And the accidental etc.: i.e., the diyat of accidental killing is one hundred camels in fifths: i.e., twenty ibn makhad (male), twenty bint makhad, twenty bint labun, twenty hiqqa, and twenty jadha'a. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/128. Because Ibn Mas‘ud [may Allah be pleased with him] reported that the Prophet [؟] said: 'In the diyat of accidental killing: twenty hiqqa, twenty jadha‘a, twenty bint makhad, twenty bint labun, and twenty ibn makhad (male).' Narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and others. And al-Shafi‘i took our madhhab except that he said: twenty ibn labun (male) must be given in place of ibn makhad, and the hadith is a proof against him. Ramz al-Haqa‘iq: 2/438.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It explains that diyat for accidental killing (khata') is 100 camels divided into five equal groups of 20 each: (1) ibn makhad (male yearling?), (2) bint makhad, (3) bint labun, (4) hiqqa, (5) jadha'a. The commentary cites a hadith from Ibn Mas‘ud listing these types, including ibn makhad (male). Imam al-Shafi‘i generally follows the Hanafi school on this but substitutes ibn labun (male) for ibn makhad. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is evidence against Shafi‘i because it explicitly includes ibn makhad. The source (Ramz al-Haqa‘iq) indicates this is the relied-upon proof.

Key Terms
ابن مخاض (ibn makhad): A male camel in its second year.
أحماس (ahmas): Plural of khums: fifths, meaning five categories of 20 each.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which male camel is included in the diyat for accidental killing?
A) Ibn labun
B) Ibn makhad
C) Jadha'a
D) Hiqqa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires twenty ibn makhad camels in diyat khata' based on the explicit hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and this serves as proof against the Shafi'i substitution with ibn labun.

The Amount of Diyat and Permissible Forms of Payment
Inter-madhhab dispute over diyat amount and intra-Hanafi dispute over permissible forms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the diyat amount (10,000 dirhams) and explain the internal dispute on permissible forms of payment (three vs. six).

Core Idea
Diyat can be paid in gold, silver, camels, and according to the sahibayn, also cows, sheep, and clothes.

The passage addresses two key questions: how much diyat must be paid in dirhams or dinars, and what types of property can be used. It first presents the Hanafi view that the amount is 10,000 dirhams (or 1,000 dinars), arguing it is more certain since it is the lesser figure. Then it reveals an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa restricts diyat to camels, gold, and silver, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also permit cows, sheep, and suits of clothes. The text explicitly chooses the disciples' view, which is also adapted to later times (e.g., a shirt and trousers instead of the traditional izar and rida').

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on amount
Identify the exact figures: 1,000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams. Note that this is the Hanafi view, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar.
The text uses 'أو ألف دينار أو عشرة آلاف درهم'.
2
Analyze the opposing view and its proof
Malik and al-Shafi‘i hold it is 12,000 dirhams, citing a hadith from Ibn Abbas. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf over the transmitted amount.
The opposing dalil is a riwayah from Ibn Abbas.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that 10,000 is more certain because it is the lesser amount (al-tayaqqun bi al-aqall). This is a methodological principle: when two reports conflict, the one yielding the lesser obligation is preferable.
The text says 'وما قلنا أولى للتيقن به؛ لأنه أقل'.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on forms
Abu Hanifa says diyat is only due from camels, gold, and silver (three types). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad add cows, sheep, and garments (hulal). Note the specific numbers: 200 cows, 2,000 sheep, 200 suits.
The text marks the sahibayn's view as 'هو المختار' (the chosen).
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its adaptation
The relied-upon view is that of the sahibayn, allowing six forms. The commentary also notes that the hulla (two garments) is interpreted in later times as a shirt and trousers.
This shows fiqh's responsiveness to customary changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو ألف دينار أو عشرة آلاف درهم وكفارتهما ما ذكر في النص، ولا يجوز الإطعام والجنين ويجوز الرضيع لو أحد أبويه مسلما، ودية المرأة على النصف . ولا تحرير الجنين لو كان أو ألف دينار إلخ أي أو ألف دينار من الذهب أو عشرة آلاف درهم من الورق، وقال مالك والشافعي: الدية اثنا عشر ألف لما روي عن ابن عباس ما أن درهم؛ رجلا قتل فجعل النبي ديته اثنى عشر ألفا، رواه أبو داود والترمذي، ولنا ما روي عن ابن عمر لما أن النبي عليه قضى بالدية في قتيل بعشرة آلاف درهم، وما قلنا أولى للتيقن به؛ لأنه أقل، ولا تكون الدية إلا من هذه الأنواع الثلاثة عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: تجب منها ومن البقر مائتا بقرة، ومن الغنم ألفا شاة، ومن الحلل مائتا حلة كل حلة ثوبان إزار ورداء هو المختار، وفي "النهاية": قيل: في زماننا قميص وسراويل رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٨/٢]
Or one thousand dinars or ten thousand dirhams, and their expiation is what is mentioned in the text. And it is not permissible (to give) food and the fetus, but the suckling child is permissible if one of its parents is Muslim. And the diyat of a woman is half. And the freeing of a fetus, if it were... Or one thousand dinars, etc.: i.e., one thousand dinars of gold or ten thousand dirhams of silver. Malik and al-Shafi‘i said: the diyat is twelve thousand dirhams due to what is narrated from Ibn Abbas: '...that a man was killed and the Prophet made his diyat twelve thousand.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. And for us (Hanafis) is what is narrated from Ibn Umar: 'the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged the diyat for a slain person as ten thousand dirhams.' And what we say is better for certainty because it is less. And diyat is only from these three types according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it becomes due from them and from cows: two hundred cows, and from sheep: two thousand sheep, and from garments (hulal): two hundred suits, each suit being two garments (izar and rida')—this is the chosen (al-mukhtar). And in al-Nihaya: it is said in our time: a shirt and trousers (qamis and sarawil). Ramz al-Haqa‘iq: 2/438.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage covers multiple issues. First, the alternative diyat in gold and silver: 1,000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams. The commentary then addresses a dispute with Malik and Shafi‘i, who say the diyat in dirhams is 12,000 based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response cites Ibn Umar's hadith that the Prophet set it at 10,000, and argues that the lesser amount is more certain (less is safer). Second, an internal Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa restricts diyat to these three types (camels, gold, silver). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (sahibayn) allow it also in cows (200 cows), sheep (2,000 sheep), and clothes (200 suits of two garments each—izar and rida'). The chosen (mukhtar) position is that of the sahibayn. The commentary notes that in later times (according to al-Nihaya), the suit is interpreted as a shirt and trousers.

Key Terms
دينار (dinar): Gold coin of specific weight (approx. 4.4g).
درهم (dirham): Silver coin of specific weight (approx. 3g).
حلة (hulla): A suit of two garments, traditionally izar and rida', later shirt and trousers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (al-mukhtar) position regarding the forms of diyat besides camels?
A) Only gold and silver (Abu Hanifa's view).
B) Gold, silver, cows, sheep, and clothes (sahibayn's view).
C) Only cows and sheep.
D) Only 10,000 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for diyat is 10,000 dirhams (or 1,000 dinars) and allows payment in camels, gold, silver, cows, sheep, or clothes, following the sahibayn's expansive view.

Kaffarah for Accidental and Quasi-Intentional Killing: Quranic Basis and Conditions
Explains the kaffarah for accidental and quasi-intentional killing from the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for accidental and quasi-intentional killing, identify its Quranic proof, and explain why feeding (it'am) and freeing a fetus are invalid, while a suckling child (rad‘i) is valid under certain conditions.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for both accidental and quasi-intentional killing is limited to freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months; no alternatives are permitted.

This lesson examines the kaffarah (expiation) required for accidental killing (qatl al-khata') and quasi-intentional killing (shibh al-amd) according to the Hanafi school. The primary source is Quran 4:92, which specifies two sequential options: freeing a believing slave, and if unable, fasting two consecutive months. The passage clarifies that feeding (it'am) is not a valid substitute, and that a fetus cannot be used for freeing because of uncertainty. However, a suckling child (rad‘i) may be freed if one of its parents is Muslim, based on the presumption of safety. The reasoning also addresses an important legal principle: a weak presumption (zahir) suffices for discharging a duty but not for imposing liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that both accidental killing (khata') and quasi-intentional killing (shibh al-amd) require kaffarah. The ruling is wajib (obligatory). Note that the kaffarah is the same for both types, unlike diyat which differs.
The basis is Quran 4:92, which mentions accidental killing, but shibh al-amd is included by qiyas because it is accidental in the killing aspect.
2
Locate the dalil and its precise content
The Quranic verse (4:92) commands: freeing a believing slave, and if not possible, fasting two consecutive months. This is the sole specification; no other substitute is mentioned.
The Hanafi principle is that fixed expiations are known only by revelation (sam'), so we cannot add other methods.
3
Understand why feeding (it'am) is invalid
Feeding is not mentioned in the Quran for this kaffarah. Since fixed obligations are determined only by revelation, introducing feeding would be an innovation.
This contrasts with kaffarah for other sins (e.g., breaking an oath) where feeding is allowed.
4
Analyze the permissibility of freeing a suckling child (rad‘i)
A suckling child can be freed if one parent is Muslim, because the child follows the Muslim parent in religion. The child's limbs are presumed safe based on natural creation (al-jibilla).
This presumption suffices for fulfilling the obligation of freeing a slave, but not for imposing liability for injury to the child's limbs.
5
Examine the objection and its resolution
An objection is raised: why is the same presumption sufficient for kaffarah but not for liability? The answer: for discharging an obligation (defrayal), a weak proof (zahir) suffices; but for imposing liability (ihqaq), certainty is needed.
This illustrates a key Hanafi principle about the strength of evidence in different contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفارتهما ما ذكر في النص، ولا يجوز الإطعام والجنين ويجوز الرضيع لو أحد أبويه مسلما، ودية المرأة على النصف . ولا تحرير الجنين [مكرر] وكفارتهما أي كفارة القتل خطأ، وشبه العمد هو الذي ذكر في القرآن وهو الإعتاق والصوم على الترتيب متتابعا لما ذكر في النص، وهو وإن كان واردا في الخطأ إلا أن شبه العمد خطأ في حق القتل، وإن كان عمدا في حق الضرب، فتتناولهما الآية، ولا يختلفان فيه لعدم النقل بالاختلاف، بخلاف الدية حيث يجب في شبه العمد مغلظة لوجود التوقيف في شبه العمد دون الخطأ، والمقادير لا تجب إلا سماعا. تكملة فتح النص: وهي: ﴿وَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ شَهْرَيْنِ مُتَتَابِعَيْنِ ﴾ (الآية) (النساء:۹۲) ولا يجوز الإطعام إلخ لأن الإطعام لم يرد به النص، والمقادير لم تعرف إلا سماعا؛ ولأن المذكور كل الواجب إما في الجواب، أو لكونه كل المذكور والجنين لم تعرف حياته ولا سلامته، فلا يجوز؛ ولأنه عضو من وجه، فلا يدخل تحت مطلق النص. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۲۹/۹] ويجوز الرضيع إلخ يعني يجوز الرضيع في الكفارة لو كان أحد أبويه مسلما؛ لأنه مسلم تبعا له والظاهر سلامة أطرافه على ما عليه الجبلة لا يقال كيف اكتفى هنا بالظاهر في سلامة أطرافه حتى جاز التكفير به، ولم يكتف بذلك في حق وجوب الضمان بإتلاف أطرافه؛ لأنا نقول: الحاجة في التكفير إلى دفع الواجب، والظاهر يصلح حجة للدفع، والحاجة في الإتلاف إلى إلزام الضمان، وهو لا يصلح حجة فيه؛ ولأنه يظهر حال الأطراف فيما بعد التكفير إذا عاش ولا كذلك في الإتلاف، فافترقا. (فتح)
And their expiation is what is mentioned in the text. And it is not permissible (to give) food and the fetus, but the suckling child is permissible if one of its parents is Muslim. And the diyat of a woman is half. And the freeing of a fetus... And their expiation, i.e., the expiation for accidental killing and quasi-intentional killing, is that which is mentioned in the Quran: freeing a believing slave and fasting consecutively in order, as mentioned in the text (Quran). And although it (the verse) came for accidental, yet quasi-intentional is accidental with respect to killing, though intentional with respect to striking, so the verse includes both. They do not differ in this due to lack of transmitted difference, unlike the diyat where it becomes heavy in quasi-intentional due to authoritative specification (tawqif) for it but not for accidental, and fixed amounts are only known by hearing. Completion of Fath: and it is: {And the freeing of a believing slave, and whoever does not find [the means] then fasting two consecutive months} (Quran 4:92). And it is not permissible to feed (it'am) etc., because feeding has not come in the text, and fixed measures are only known by hearing. And because what is mentioned is the entirety of what is obligatory either in the answer or because it is all that is mentioned. And the fetus (janin) is not known to be alive nor safe, so it is not permissible. And because it is a limb in one sense, so it does not fall under the unrestricted text. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 9/129. And the suckling child is permissible, meaning that it is permissible to use a suckling child in kaffarah if one of his parents is Muslim, because he is Muslim by following him, and the apparent (zahir) safety of his limbs is as per natural creation. It cannot be said: how is the apparent (zahir) sufficient here for safety of limbs such that kaffarah is permitted, while it is not sufficient in the case of liability for destruction of limbs? We reply: The need in kaffarah is to discharge an obligation, and the apparent is a sufficient proof for discharging; but the need in destruction is to impose liability, and the apparent is not a proof for that. And because the condition of limbs becomes apparent after the kaffarah if it (the child) lives, not so in destruction, so they differ. (Fath)
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage covers the kaffarah (expiation) for accidental (khata') and quasi-intentional (shibh al-amd) killing. The kaffarah is the same for both: freeing a believing slave, if possible; otherwise, fasting two consecutive months, as per Quran 4:92. The verse mentions only these two options; it'am (feeding) is not allowed because it is not in the text, and fixed expiations are known only by revelation. Also, a fetus cannot be freed because its life and safety are unknown. However, a suckling child (rad‘i) can be used if one of its parents is Muslim, as it is Muslim by following the parent and its limbs are presumed safe. The commentary also addresses a potential objection: why is the presumption of safety sufficient for kaffarah but not for imposing liability for injuries? The answer is that kaffarah is about discharging an obligation, where presumption suffices, while imposing liability requires certainty.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for sinful actions; here for killing.
رضيع (rad‘i): A suckling child who is still breastfeeding.
خطأ (khata'): Accidental killing.
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Quasi-intentional killing: intentional striking but accidental death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school not allow feeding (it'am) as kaffarah for accidental killing?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because feeding is only for fasting.
C) Because the scholars did not agree.
D) Because it is too easy.

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah for accidental and quasi-intentional killing is exclusively freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months, as per Quran 4:92; no other form of expiation, such as feeding, is acceptable.

8 min
Killing by a Minor or Insane Person: Treated as Accidental
Ruling on intentional killing by a child or insane person treated as khata.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that the intentional killing by a child or insane person is treated as accidental, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by citing the evidence and the practical consequences.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school treats intentional killing by a child or insane person as accidental, so diyah falls on the 'aqila and no kaffarah or disinheritance applies.

This lesson addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the legal classification of homicide committed by a child or an insane person. While both agree qisas (retaliation) is not applicable, they differ on diyah, expiation, and inheritance. The Hanafi position, based on a narration from 'Ali (ra) and rational analogy, treats such acts as accidental, placing the burden on the 'aqila. We will examine the proofs and the practical implications of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the intentional killing is treated as accidental (khata'); consequence: diyah on the 'aqila, no kaffarah, no disinheritance.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds it is intentional for all purposes except qisas; diyah from killer's own wealth, kaffarah obligatory, and disinheritance applies.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues the act is intentional in reality; only qisas is dropped, so the other rulings (diyah in own wealth, kaffarah, disinheritance) remain.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: intentionality requires intellect; the insane lack it, the child has deficient intellect, so their act is like a sleeping person. Narration from 'Ali (ra) equates the insane's intentional and accidental.
This is a dalil naqli supported by qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi – diyah on 'aqila, no kaffarah, killer inherits; Shafi'i – diyah from killer, kaffarah, disinherited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعمد الصبي والمجنون خطأ، وديته على عاقلته ولا تكفير فيه ولا حرمان، والمعتوه في حكم الخطأ دية عمد الصبي قتلهما عمدا عن الإرث كالصبي.. في الحكم المذكور وعمد الصبي إلخ: أي إذا قتل صبي أو مجنون رجلا عمدا، فحكمه حكم الخطأ، فيجب ديته على عاقلته؛ لما روي عن علي الله أنه جعل عقل المجنون على عاقلته وقال: "عمده وخطأه سواء"؛ ولأن الصبي مظنة العذر، والعاقل الخاطئ لما استحق التخفيف حتى وجبت الدية على العاقلة، فالصبي أحق بهذه التخفيف، وقال الشافعي: عمدهما عمد حتى تجب الدية في مالهما؛ إذ العمد هو القصد غير أنه تخلف عنه أحد حكميه، وهو القصاص، فينسحب عليه حكمه الآخر، وهو الوجوب في ماله، ولهذا تجب الكفارة، ويحرم عن الميراث على أصله؛ لأنهما يتعلقان بالقتل ولنا ما قدمنا ولا نسلم تحقق العمدية فإنها تترتب على العلم والعلم بالعقل، والمجنون عديم العقل، والصبي قاصر العقل، فأنى يتحقق منهما القصد، فصار كالنائم. (فتح) ولا تكفير فيه إلخ أي لا كفارة على الصبي والمجنون، ولا يحرمان عن الميراث بالقتل عندنا؛ لأن الكفارة كاسمها ستارة ولا ذنب تستره؛ لأنهما مرفوعا القلم، وحرمان الإرث عقوبة وهما ليس من أهلها، وأما حرمان الصبي المرتد من ميراث أبيه، فلاختلاف الدين لا جزاء للردة، وفيه خلاف الشافعي كما مر. (فتح وغيره بتصرف)
And the deliberate [killing] by a child and an insane person is [treated as] accidental, and its diyah is upon his 'aqila, and there is no expiation therein nor deprivation [of inheritance], and the insane person is in the ruling of accidental. The diyah of the intentional killing of a child... killing them both intentionally... from inheritance... like the child... in the aforementioned ruling. And 'the deliberate by a child etc.': i.e., if a child or insane person intentionally kills a man, its ruling is the ruling of accidental, so his diyah is obligatory upon his 'aqila; because of what was narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he made the 'aql of the insane person upon his 'aqila and said: 'His intentional and his accidental are the same.' And because the child is a seat of excuse, and the rational mistaken person, when he deserved leniency such that the diyah became obligatory upon the 'aqila, so the child is more deserving of this leniency. Al-Shafi'i said: Their intentional [act] is intentional, so the diyah is obligatory upon their wealth, because intentionality is the intention, except that one of its two rulings, namely retaliation, is dropped, so its other ruling, namely obligation upon his wealth, applies; and for this reason expiation is obligatory, and he is deprived of inheritance according to his principle, because both are connected to killing. And our [proof] is what we have presented, and we do not accept the realization of intentionality, for it is based on knowledge, and knowledge is based on intellect; the insane person lacks intellect, and the child has deficient intellect, so how can they have intentionality? So they are like a sleeping person. (Fath) And 'no expiation therein etc.': i.e., there is no expiation upon the child and insane person, and they are not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us; because expiation, as its name implies, is a covering, and there is no sin to cover, because the pen is lifted from them; and deprivation of inheritance is a punishment, and they are not among its people. As for the deprivation of an apostate child from his father's inheritance, it is because of difference of religion, not a penalty for apostasy, and there is a difference with al-Shafi'i regarding it as has passed. (Fath and others with modification)
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal treatment of intentional killing by a child or an insane person. The matn states that such killing is treated as accidental (khata'), so the diyah (blood money) is upon the 'aqila (tribal insurers), and no kaffarah (expiation) is required nor does the killer lose his right to inheritance from the victim. The commentary expands: if a child or insane person intentionally kills someone, the ruling is that of accidental killing. The proof is a narration from 'Ali (ra) that he made the 'aql of the insane person upon his 'aqila and said, 'His intentional and his accidental are the same.' Additionally, the child is a prime candidate for excuse; since a rational person who kills by mistake is given leniency (diyah on 'aqila), the child is even more deserving. Al-Shafi'i opposes: he considers their intentional act as true intentional, so the diyah is to be paid from their own wealth (not the 'aqila) because the essence of intentionality is present; only the retaliation (qisas) is dropped, but the other ruling (obligation of diyah upon them) remains. Consequently, expiation is also obligatory, and the killer is deprived of inheritance. The Hanafi response is that we do not accept the existence of genuine intentionality for them, since intention requires knowledge, which requires intellect; the insane have no intellect and the child has deficient intellect, so their act is like that of a sleeping person. The passage further clarifies that no expiation is due because the pen is lifted from them (they are not accountable), and they are not disinherited because that is a punishment for accountable adults. The exception of an apostate child is due to difference of religion.

Key Terms
عمد الصبي والمجنون ('amd al-ṣabī wa al-majnūn): The deliberate act of killing by a child (who has not reached puberty) or an insane person; legally treated as a mistake in the Hanafi school.
عاقلة ('āqila): The group of paternal relatives (tribe or clan) liable for paying diyah on behalf of the killer in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional killing.
كفارة (kaffāra): Expiation required for certain sins; here, for intentional killing. In this context, not required for child or insane killer due to lack of accountability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on whom is the diyah obligatory when a child intentionally kills someone?
A) The child's own wealth
B) The child's 'aqila
C) The state treasury
D) The child's father

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the intentional killing by a child or insane person is treated as accidental, placing diyah on the 'aqila and exempting the killer from kaffarah and disinheritance.

Compensation for Causing Miscarriage: Ghurrah, Diyah, and Disputes
Ruling with proof on miscarriage compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for compensation for causing a miscarriage, identify the proofs from hadith and qiyas, and explain the dispute with the Maliki school regarding the 'aqila.

Core Idea
For causing a stillbirth, ghurrah (500 dirhams) is obligatory on the 'aqila, based on the Prophetic hadith overriding qiyas.

This lesson explores the rulings for causing a miscarriage (janin). The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith and istihsan, establishes a fixed compensation (ghurrah) for a stillborn fetus. We will examine the proof, the qiyas that would leave no compensation, and the inter-madhhab disagreement with Imam Malik regarding who pays.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Striking a woman's belly causing miscarriage) and what is the compensation? (ghurrah: half a tenth of diyah).
The ghurrah is 500 dirhams for both male and female fetus due to diyah of woman being half.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the woman from Hudhayl is the primary proof: the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam) ruled a ghurrah for the fetus and placed it on the 'aqila.
This hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Compare with qiyas
Qiyas with a confirmed human life would require no compensation because the life of the fetus is not certain. This underscores the importance of the hadith.
The hadith overrides qiyas through istihsan.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to Malik
Imam Malik argued the ghurrah is on the perpetrator's wealth because it compensates a part. The Hanafi school responds that the hadith explicitly places it on the 'aqila, and it is like a life compensation in one respect.
The thamarah al-khilaf: 'aqila pays in Hanafi, perpetrator pays in Maliki.
5
Apply to complex scenarios
If the fetus is born alive then dies, full diyah is due. If multiple stillborn fetuses, multiple ghurrahs. If mother also dies, both diyah and ghurrah are due because the act multiplies by effects.
The principle: the act multiplies by its effects (tata'addada bi ta'addud al-athar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في الجنين [هو اسم الولد في بطن الأم قبل أن يولد فإذا ولد يسمى وليدا ثم رضيعا على ما عرف في موضعه] لما كان الجنين في حكم الجزء من الكل ذكر أحكامه عقيب أحكام الأجزاء الحقيقية، والجنين فعيل بمعنى مفعول من جنّه إذا ستره، وهو الولد ما دام في الرحم سمي به لاجتنانه أي استتاره في البطن. (من الفتح وغيره) ضرب بطن امرأة فألقت جنينا ميتا تجب غرة، وهي نصف عشر الدية، فإن ألقته حيا فمات فدية، وإن ألقت ميتا فماتت الأم، فدية وغرة، جنينا حيا الجنين أي تجب دية كاملة جنينا الشيء وهي كاملة بالأم بالجنين المرأة. غرة بضم الغين المعجمة وتشديد الراء وغرة الشيء في اللغة: خياره كالفرس النجيب والحمار الفاره، وغرة ء أوله كما . سمي أول الشهر غرة، وسمي وجه الإنسان غرة؛ لأنه أول شيء يظهر. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٦/٢] نصف : ، أراد نصف عشر دية الرجل إذا كان الجنين ذكرا، وعشر دية المرأة إذا كان أنثى، وكل منهما خمسمائة درهم؛ لأن دية المرأة نصف دية الرجل، والأصل فيه ما روي أن امرأة من هذيل ضربت بطن امرأة بحجر فقتلتها، وما في بطنها، فاختصموا إلى رسول الله ، فقضى أن دية جنينها غرة عبد أو وليدة، وقضى بدية المرأة على عاقلتها"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وهي على العاقلة عندنا. وعند مالك في ماله؛ لأنه بدل الجزء، ولنا: أنه عليه قضى بالغرة على العاقلة ولأنه بدل النفس من وجه، وتجب في سنة عندنا، وعند الشافعي: في ثلاث سنين؛ لأنه بدل النفس، ألا ترى أنه يورث، ولنا: ما روي عن الحسن أنه قال: بلغنا أن رسول الله اول قضى بالغرة على العاقلة في سنة رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٦/٢] وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه يتيقن بحياته، والظاهر لا يصلح حجة للاستحقاق، لكن تركناه بالأثر، وهو حجة على من قدرها بست مائة نحو مالك والشافعي. عيني هداية فإن ألقته حيا إلخ: أي تحب دية كاملة؛ لأنه أتلف آدميا خطأ أو شبه عمد، فتجب فيه الدية تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٤/٩] محمد بن فدية وغرة لما ،روينا ولأنهما جنايتان، فيجب فيهما موجبهما، وهذا لما عرف أن الفعل يتعدد بتعدد أثره، فصار كما إذا رمى فأصاب شخصا ونفذت منه إلى آخر فقتله فإنه يجب عليه ديتان ولو ألقت ميتين أو أكثر، تعددت الغرة كما في "الذخيرة"، وفي "الدر" عن البزازية: ضرب بطن امرأة بالسيف فألقت جنينا حيا، وآخر ميتا، وبه جراحة السيف وماتت أيضا، يقتص لأجل المرأة وعلى عاقلته دية الولد الحي إذا مات، وتجب غرة الولد الميت؛ لأنه لما ضرب ولم يعلم بالولدين في بطنها كان الضرب خطأ. (تكملة، فتح)
Chapter on the fetus [It is the name of the child in the mother's womb before it is born; when it is born, it is called a walid, then a radi', as known in its place.] Since the fetus is in the ruling of a part of the whole, its rulings were mentioned after the rulings of the actual parts. Al-janīn is fa‘īl in the sense of maf‘ūl from janna, meaning to cover; it is the child as long as it is in the womb, named for its concealment in the belly. (From al-Fatḥ and others) He struck a woman's belly and she miscarried a dead fetus: a ghurrah is obligatory, which is half a tenth of the diyah. If she gives birth to it alive and it dies, then a diyah. If she miscarries dead and the mother dies, then a diyah and a ghurrah. A fetus alive... the fetus i.e. a complete diyah obligatory... the thing... and it is complete... by the mother... by the fetus... the woman. Ghurrah, with a ḍammah on the ghayn and tashdīd of the rā'. Linguistically, ghurrah of a thing: its best, like a noble horse or a fine donkey. [Another definition] The first of the month is called ghurrah, and the face of a man is called ghurrah because it is the first thing that appears. [Rumūz al-Ḥaqā’iq: 2/446] Half: meaning half of a tenth of the diyah of a man if the fetus is male, and a tenth of the diyah of a woman if it is female, and each is five hundred dirhams, because the diyah of a woman is half the diyah of a man. The basis for this is what was narrated: a woman from Hudhayl struck a pregnant woman's belly with a stone, killing her and what was in her belly; they brought the case to the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), and he ruled that the diyah for her fetus is a ghurrah: a male or female slave, and he ruled the diyah of the woman upon her ‘āqila.” Reported by Bukhārī and Muslim. And it is upon the ‘āqila according to us. According to Mālik, it is upon his own wealth because it is compensation for a part. Our proof: that he (ﷺ) ruled the ghurrah upon the ‘āqila, and because it is compensation for a life in one respect. It is due in one year according to us. According to al-Shāfi‘ī, it is due in three years because it is compensation for a life, so it is inherited. Our proof: what was narrated from al-Ḥasan that he said: it reached us that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) ruled the ghurrah upon the ‘āqila in one year. [Rumūz al-Ḥaqā’iq: 2/446] This is istiḥsān; the qiyās would be that nothing is obligatory because the life of the fetus is not certain, and the apparent is not sufficient as proof for entitlement, but we left qiyās due to the athar (tradition). This athar is evidence against those who estimate it as six hundred [dirhams], like Mālik and al-Shāfi‘ī. [‘Ayn al-Hidāyah?] Then: 'If she gives birth to it alive etc.': i.e., a complete diyah is obligatory because he destroyed a human being by mistake or quasi-intentional, so diyah is obligatory for it. [Takmilat al-Baḥr al-Rā’iq: 9/154] Muhammad ibn... 'Diyah and ghurrah' – because of what we narrated, and because they are two injuries, so the consequences of each are obligatory. This is because it is known that the act multiplies by its effects, so it becomes like when a person shoots, hits one person, and the arrow penetrates and hits another, killing him; then two diyahs are obligatory. And if she miscarries two or more [dead], the ghurrahs multiply, as in al-Dhakhīra. In al-Durr from al-Bazzāziyya: He struck a woman's belly with a sword, and she gave birth to a live fetus and a dead one, and there was a wound from the sword, and she also died; retaliation is required for the woman, and upon his ‘āqila is the diyah of the live child if it dies, and the ghurrah of the dead child is obligatory; because when he struck and did not know about the two fetuses in her belly, the strike was a mistake. (Takmila, Fatḥ)
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (bab) on the fetus (janin), presenting a series of rulings with proofs and inter-madhhab disputes. The chapter begins by defining the fetus as a child in the womb, and explains why its rulings follow those of bodily parts (since it is considered a part of the mother). The main ruling: if a person strikes a pregnant woman's belly causing a stillbirth, a ghurrah is obligatory. The ghurrah is defined as half a tenth of the full diyah – five hundred dirhams for a male fetus (half a tenth of a man's diyah) and for a female fetus, a tenth of a woman's diyah (which is also five hundred dirhams, since woman's diyah is half). This is based on the hadith of the woman from Hudhayl, recorded in Bukhari and Muslim, where the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam) ruled that the compensation for the fetus is a ghurrah (a male or female slave). The Hanafi position holds that this ghurrah is upon the 'aqila (tribal insurers), based on the Prophetic ruling. Imam Malik disagreed, arguing it is upon the perpetrator's own wealth because it is compensation for a part. The Hanafi response is that the hadith explicitly places it on the 'aqila, and also it is compensation for a life in one respect. Regarding the payment term, the Hanafi school holds it is due in one year, while al-Shafi'i says three years because it is like diyah for a life and can be inherited. The Hanafi proof is a report from al-Hasan al-Basri that the Prophet ruled it in one year. The text notes that this ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), as qiyas would require certainty of life which is lacking, but the tradition overrides it. The passage then covers further cases: if the fetus is born alive and then dies, a full diyah is obligatory (because a human life was destroyed). If the mother also dies, both a full diyah for the mother and a ghurrah for the fetus are due, because the act multiplies by its effects, analogized to an arrow hitting two persons. For multiple stillborn fetuses, multiple ghurrahs are due. A final example from al-Bazzaziyya involves a woman struck with a sword, giving birth to one live and one stillborn fetus, with the mother dying: qisas for the mother, diyah for the live child if it dies, and ghurrah for the stillborn, because the strike was a mistake due to ignorance of multiple fetuses.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurra): Compensation for a miscarriage: half a tenth of the diyah (500 dirhams for a male or female fetus), originally a valuable slave.
جنين (janīn): The child in the womb from conception until birth; considered legally as a part of the mother for purposes of diyat.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; here used to prefer the hadith over qiyas (analogy) when the latter would lead to no compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a fetus is born alive and then dies due to an injury, what compensation is required?
A) A ghurrah (half a tenth of diyah)
B) A full diyah
C) Nothing, because it was not certain to survive
D) One tenth of diyah

Key Takeaway
For causing a miscarriage, the Hanafi school obligates ghurrah (500 dirhams) on the 'aqila based on the hadith, overriding qiyas via istihsan.
